GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.8817*A**2 + 0.5985*sin(sqrt(A))`

The key components are:
1. A term proportional to `A²`
2. A term involving `sin(√A)` = `sin(A^(1/2))`

The `sin(√A)` term is highly specific and non-standard. Let me check if any candidate can reproduce this.

**Critical observation:** `sin(√A)` cannot be expressed as a finite combination of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, rational functions, or `sin` of polynomial/linear arguments of A. It requires `sin` applied to a non-linear, non-polynomial function of A (specifically `√A`).

Let me scan for candidates containing `sin`:

- **Candidate 15:** `... + c6*sin(c7*log(A²*c8 + 1) + c9)` — This has `sin(c7*log(c8*A²+1) + c9)`. Can `c7*log(c8*A²+1)` equal `√A`? No, `log` of a polynomial cannot equal `√A` for all A.

- **Candidate 43:** `A³*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*exp(A²*c6)` — This has `sin(c3*A + c4)`, a sine of a linear function of A. This cannot equal `sin(√A)` for all A.

Now let me check if any candidate has `A**c` terms that could give `sin(√A)` behavior. No — `A**c` is a power function, not a sine.

Let me reconsider: could any candidate approximate or exactly match the GT through some algebraic identity I'm missing?

The GT has `sin(√A)`. None of the candidates contain `sin(√A)` or any mechanism to produce it. The only `sin` appearances are in candidates 15 and 43, neither of which can produce `sin(√A)`.

Could `sin(√A)` be expressed using exponentials, logs, or other functions present in the candidates? No — `sin(√A)` is a transcendental function that cannot be written as a finite combination of `exp`, `log`, polynomials, or rational functions of A.

Wait — could `tanh` or other functions somehow combine? No, `tanh` is a hyperbolic function and cannot produce oscillatory `sin` behavior.

Let me also check candidate 34 which has `A**c3` terms — these are power-law terms, not sine.

Candidates with `A**c` terms (like 1, 4, 9, 18, 21, 25, 27, 37, 40, 41): These have `c*A^c` which is a power of A, not `sin(√A)`.

**Conclusion:** The function `sin(√A)` is a fundamentally distinct transcendental function that cannot be represented by any finite combination of the building blocks available in the candidates (polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, rational functions, `sin` of linear/polynomial arguments, `tanh`, power functions `A^c`). None of the candidates can match the GT.

[NO MATCH]

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A)**

The GT consists of two basis functions: **A²** and **sin(√A)**. There is no dependence on **t**.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The key question for each is: can it produce exactly the form `c*A² + d*sin(√A)`?

**Key observations:**
- The GT has **sin(√A)** — a very specific transcendental function
- Most candidates use **exp**, **log**, **tanh**, **rational functions**, or **polynomial** terms — none of which can produce sin(√A)
- sin(√A) cannot be represented by any finite combination of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, or rational functions
- Only candidates containing **sin** (or equivalent trigonometric functions) have any chance

Let me identify candidates with **sin** or trigonometric functions:

- **Candidate 15**: has `c6*sin(c7*log(A²*c8 + 1) + c9)` — argument is `c7*log(c8*A²+1) + c9`, not √A. Can we set this equal to √A? No, log(c8*A²+1) ≠ √A for all A.
- **Candidate 24**: has `c5*tanh(c6*t + c7)` — tanh, not sin; and depends on t (can zero it, but then no sin term)
- **Candidate 27**: has `c5*tanh(c6*t + c7)` — same issue
- **Candidate 33**: has `c5*exp(c6/(c7+t))` and `c8*log(A²*c9+1)` — no sin
- **Candidate 43**: has `c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)` — argument is linear in A, i.e., sin(c3*A + c4). This is NOT sin(√A). sin(c3*A + c4) ≠ sin(√A) for all A.
- **Candidate 50**: has `c5*tanh(c6*t + c7)` and `c8*log(A²*c9+1)` — no sin(√A)

**None of the candidates contain sin(√A) or any expression that can be algebraically transformed into sin(√A).**

Let me verify there's no hidden way to get sin(√A):
- exp, log, polynomials, rational functions, tanh — none can produce sin
- sin(linear in A) ≠ sin(√A)
- sin(log(...)) ≠ sin(√A)
- A^c with fractional c gives power functions, not sin(√A)

Every candidate either lacks a sin term entirely, or has sin with the wrong argument. Since sin(√A) is linearly independent from all other basis functions present in these candidates, none can match.
